  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ca36fe75-d999-4021-b7d1-017df533254d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16105458413342288244"><b>An instant bestseller in Spain, with rights sold in twenty-eight countries and counting, <i>God’s Spy</i> is a spectacular contemporary thriller set in the Vatican, where, in the aftermath of Pope John Paul II’s death, the hunt for a serial killer reveals a chilling conspiracy.</b> <p> In the days following the Pope’s death, a cardinal is found brutally murdered in a chapel in Rome, his</p></span>
  <span id="freeText16105458413342288244" style="display:none"><b>An instant bestseller in Spain, with rights sold in twenty-eight countries and counting, <i>God’s Spy</i> is a spectacular contemporary thriller set in the Vatican, where, in the aftermath of Pope John Paul II’s death, the hunt for a serial killer reveals a chilling conspiracy.</b> <p> In the days following the Pope’s death, a cardinal is found brutally murdered in a chapel in Rome, his eyes gouged and his hands cut off. Called in for the grisly case, police inspector Paola Dicanti learns that another cardinal was recently found dead; he had also been tortured. Desperate to find the killer before another victim dies, Paola’s investigation is soon joined by Father Anthony Fowler—an American priestand former Army intelligence officer examining sexual abuse in the Church, who knows far more about the killer than Paola could possibly imagine. </p><p> As Paola and Father Anthony struggle through a maze of tantalizing clues, they begin to question whether someone in the Vatican is aiding their cause or abetting a murderer. And when evidence leads them to powerful figures within the Church hierarchy, their own pursuit of the truth may make them the next pawns to be sacrificed in a terrifying and deadly game. </p><p> A dazzling, impossible-to-put-down thriller, Juan Gómez-Jurado’s <i>God’s Spy</i> marks the arrival of a major new talent to the contemporary suspense fiction scene.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="16105458413342288244" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3270332692?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3270332692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5996605814725164746">Pope John II has died. The cardinals are gathering in Rome for the conclave. A grisly murder is discovered of one of the cardinals, but he was not the first victim. The case is assigned to one of a few profilers in the world, Italian Inspector Paola Dicanti of the Laboratory for Behavioral Analysis (LAC). The Vatican Police Force and her boss, Carlo Troi, Director General of the Department for the Analysis of Violent Crime (UAVC), do not want the murders to be publicized during this critical tim</span>
  <span id="freeText5996605814725164746" style="display:none">Pope John II has died. The cardinals are gathering in Rome for the conclave. A grisly murder is discovered of one of the cardinals, but he was not the first victim. The case is assigned to one of a few profilers in the world, Italian Inspector Paola Dicanti of the Laboratory for Behavioral Analysis (LAC). The Vatican Police Force and her boss, Carlo Troi, Director General of the Department for the Analysis of Violent Crime (UAVC), do not want the murders to be publicized during this critical time as millions have descended upon and are viewing the wake, funeral, and election in Vatican City, and each pushes its own agenda. Working with Fabio Dante, a Deputy Inspector of the Vatican Police Force; Priest Anthony Fowler, a former officer in the U.S. Air Force Intelligence; Detective Maurizio Pontiero; and Forensic Sculptor and Digital Image Expert Angelo Biffi, they quickly identify the killer, Victor Korosky, a former priest. Tensions arise among the team as egos clash, boundaries are pushed, and information is limited. However, Victor toys with them as he flaunts his presence, commits further atrocities, and disappears before he can be caught. Pursuing the truth has dangerous consequences as evidence is uncovered that they may be merely pawns in the election of the next pope. The plot is fast moving and the characters realistic with their flaws and all. An enjoyable and intriguing read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5996605814725164746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3394314842223432457">GOD’S SPY (Police Proc-Insp. Paola Dicanti-Rome-Cont) - VG<br/>Gómez-Jurado, Juan – 1st novel<br/>Plume, 2007, US Trade Paperback – ISBN: 9780452289123<br/><br/>First Sentence: Father Selznick awoke in the middle of the night, a fish knife pressed against his throat.<br/><br/>Pope John Paul II has died and cardinals are gathering from around the world.   <span id="freeText3394314842223432457" style="display:none">GOD’S SPY (Police Proc-Insp. Paola Dicanti-Rome-Cont) - VG<br />Gómez-Jurado, Juan – 1st novel<br />Plume, 2007, US Trade Paperback – ISBN: 9780452289123<br /><br />First Sentence: Father Selznick awoke in the middle of the night, a fish knife pressed against his throat.<br /><br />Pope John Paul II has died and cardinals are gathering from around the world. In the midst of the world’s eye on Rome, Police Inspector Paola Dicanti is faced with a dead, mutilated cardinal, a charismatic American priest with a complicated past, the head of the Vatican Police whose job is to avoid any controversy falling on the Church and a serial killer taunting them all.<br /><br />The fact that you know the killer from the beginning does nothing to diminish the excitement or complexity of this story. The book includes a Cast of Characters at the beginning and even a map, two things I appreciate, but I found the story was so well told and the characters so well developed, I didn’t need either element. <br /><br />Dicanti, as a female Inspector trained by the FBI in criminal profiling yet still living with her mother, is a wonderful character. The story is fast-paced, does include some graphic descriptions of the murders, has touches of humor, plenty of violence, psychological suspense and a couple excellent twists. <br /><br />Highly recommended. <br /></span>

<div id="review_20499181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20499181" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/582249-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193504228p2/582249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20499181?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/582249-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/582249-jen?shelf=police-fiction">police-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/582249-jen?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20499181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10132659605122494040">In this novel, Paola Dicanti, an FBI-trained profiler working in Rome, is called in when a prominent Catholic Cardinal is brutally murdered and dismembered. When Paola discovers that this is actually the second cardinal killed in this fashion, she's on the trail of a serial killer...a serial killer killing cardinals in Rome in the midst of John Paul IIs funeral and the impending conclave to elect a new Pope.<br/><br/>I listened to this book on CD in my car, and I have to say that the reader did not do the</span>
  <span id="freeText10132659605122494040" style="display:none">In this novel, Paola Dicanti, an FBI-trained profiler working in Rome, is called in when a prominent Catholic Cardinal is brutally murdered and dismembered. When Paola discovers that this is actually the second cardinal killed in this fashion, she's on the trail of a serial killer...a serial killer killing cardinals in Rome in the midst of John Paul IIs funeral and the impending conclave to elect a new Pope.<br /><br />I listened to this book on CD in my car, and I have to say that the reader did not do the book justice. This was a great book and the reader was not "great". But that aside, the plot was original and captivating. I may have to go back and physically read the book, however, because at the end I felt like I missed something. I don't know if I wasn't paying close enough attention while I was listening, or if the end was just vague and you weren't supposed to completely understand it. <br /><br />I thought the "romantic" episode between Paola and Anthony Fowler was cliche. But cliches definitely didn't abound in this novel. <br /><br />The first about two-thirds of the book left me guessing and constantly trying to fit the pieces together. Once Paola completed her profile of Victor, however, the remainder of the novel seemed a bit on the predictable side.<br /><br />Gomez-Jurado's character development was good as well. Since I was listening on audio book, it took me a little while to establish who each character was, but once I did, it wasn't hard to follow at all. Paola is sometimes stereotypical (i.e., the single female who sleeps with her married boss), but not completely. She has the makings of a strong female protagonist if Gomez-Jurado continues this as a series. But Anthony Fowler exhibited the most dynamic characteristics. I found that it was his character I wanted to know more about and delve into.<br /><br />There were points where Gomez-Jurado seemed to overdo the crass language. It really diminishes a character when that's the best they can do as far as dialogue or monologue. But overall, I thoroughly enjoyed this novel and was definitely captivated by it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10132659605122494040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_100016082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100016082" />
    <a title="Book Concierge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge"><img alt="Book Concierge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324904606p2/1628041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100016082?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Book Concierge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Book Concierge" href="/user/show/1628041-book-concierge">Book Concierge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1628041-book-concierge?shelf=italy">italy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer100016082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16111070568245487641">This sounded like a great novel, but it’s really not much more than a rip off of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/960.Angels___Demons__Robert_Langdon___1_' title='Angels & Demons (Robert Langdon, #1) by Dan Brown' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angels & Demons</a> by Daniel Brown. The Pope has died and as the cardinals gather in Vatican City to prepare to elect the successor, some crazed killer begins to kill some of the leading candidates to succeed as Pontiff.<br/><br/>What’s different from A&D? No great secret society is behind anything. The killer is a sociopathic deranged (former) priest who <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[also abused children back in Boston, and who was, himself, </span></span>
  <span id="freeText16111070568245487641" style="display:none">This sounded like a great novel, but it’s really not much more than a rip off of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/960.Angels___Demons__Robert_Langdon___1_" title="Angels &amp; Demons (Robert Langdon, #1) by Dan Brown" rel="nofollow noopener">Angels &amp; Demons</a> by Daniel Brown. The Pope has died and as the cardinals gather in Vatican City to prepare to elect the successor, some crazed killer begins to kill some of the leading candidates to succeed as Pontiff.<br /><br />What’s different from A&amp;D? No great secret society is behind anything. The killer is a sociopathic deranged (former) priest who <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[also abused children back in Boston, and who was, himself, abused by his own father. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The lead man is also a priest – who was also in the CIA. And, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[unlike most heroes – he will die in the end. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> There is no real love interest (although there is some subtle sexual tension <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[between the woman detective and the CIA priest). <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The author’s attempt to include the background of the killer through flashbacks to his time in a psychiatric facility for wayward priests falls short of the mark. He doesn’t really explain anything and leaves way too many questions for the non-psychology major. His introduction of the inexperienced but smart and intuitive Spanish journalist showed promise – but he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[basically “killed” her off and no more is heard from her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The story, of course, will never be made known because it is not in the interests of the Holy Mother Church to have the public be aware of these issues/problems. And, of course, the Rome police will go along with this. <br /><br />It’s a fast read and a decent enough thriller, but he’s no Dan Brown. <br /><br />As we prepare for our book discussion, the fact that the scandal of sex-abuse by priests supposedly known by and covered up by our current pontiff (Benedict XVI, the former Cardinal Ratzinger of Munich) adds an interesting dimension. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16111070568245487641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2245150714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2245150714" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1478144-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450473p2/1478144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2245150714?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/1478144-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2245150714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer928076152574346398">This will have to be quick, but it's been a while since last I enjoyed a thriller so much.<br/><br/>It's 2005 and Pope John Paul II has just died. Gazillions of the faithful gather in Vatican City for the funeral, as do over a hundred cardinals to elect John Paul's successor. But a serial killer has begun knocking off the cardinals in a most gruesome fashion. Italian cop/profiler Paola Dicanti and CIA agent/priest Anthony Fowler investigate, all the while being hampered by the Vatican's desire to keep the</span>
  <span id="freeText928076152574346398" style="display:none">This will have to be quick, but it's been a while since last I enjoyed a thriller so much.<br /><br />It's 2005 and Pope John Paul II has just died. Gazillions of the faithful gather in Vatican City for the funeral, as do over a hundred cardinals to elect John Paul's successor. But a serial killer has begun knocking off the cardinals in a most gruesome fashion. Italian cop/profiler Paola Dicanti and CIA agent/priest Anthony Fowler investigate, all the while being hampered by the Vatican's desire to keep the crimes a secret from the world.<br /><br />The killer's identity is revealed early on, which you might think would reduce the suspense quotient a tad. Not a bit of it. If anything it actually ramps it up, because we know -- as of course do Dicanti and Fowler -- that there are undercurrents presently invisible to us that may, on being revealed, change entirely our perception of what's going on.<br /><br />The book's not perfect. The translation lumbers from time to time, and has occasional little errors that the copyeditor should have picked up. (The proofreading's a bit sloppy too.) The denouement's arguably a bit rushed. There's some cheesy testosterone-fueled squabbling among the males around Ducanti. But I happily forgave all of that. A great read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="928076152574346398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780452289123" href="/book/show/2570470-god-s-spy">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1126891-j?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17275919593036947155">pg 83-84 " <i>... You don't think I'm in a little bit over my head with all this ?"...<br/>Troi's fingers stroked his chin. He forced Dicanti to look directly at him. <br/>"We're all in a little bit over our heads, bambina. But let all of that go. Just focus on the fact that there's a monster killing people.   <span id="freeText17275919593036947155" style="display:none">pg 83-84 " <i>... You don't think I'm in a little bit over my head with all this ?"...<br />Troi's fingers stroked his chin. He forced Dicanti to look directly at him. <br />"We're all in a little bit over our heads, bambina. But let all of that go. Just focus on the fact that there's a monster killing people. And your job is hunting monsters."<br />Paola smiled. She was grateful and she wanted him again, one last time, right there, even though she knew it was a mistake, and it would break her heart...</i>"<br /><br />Hmmm, this could get to be a little much...<br />Nearly every time our heroine encounters a man in this book--- and that happens all the time, possibly due to the fact that she's working in the context of The Vatican -- little romantic bells go off, and she tries to tell herself not to be so attracted, for once. Settle down, Paola, it's not all what it seems.<br /><br />Who is Paola Dicanti ? She's a two-fisted FBI-trained profiler who carries a couple of handguns, and would rather get in a scuffle than let down her principles; she's tough but sensitive and has a sixth sense for sniffing out serial killers. She slaps her boss and sleeps with a priest. She's Just Amazing. <br /><br />This is pretty awful, and only manages to keep the reader involved with its nonstop plot developments. Even with all the dismembering and eye-gouging going on, it still arranges to ridicule Jodie Foster and Hannibal Lecter --by name-- while navigating that same and heavily-plowed turf.<br /><br />The only parts I found to be interesting were the offhand description of Vatican particulars that wouldn't be seen by the usual visitor. As in a description of the building used to house the Cardinals choosing a new Pope during the Conclave :<br /><br /><i>The Domus Sanctae Marthae, St. Martha's House. Located to the west of the basilica, inside the walls of the Vatican. From outside it's apearance was austere. Straight, elegant lines, without moldings, adornment, or statues ... [but] the inside bore little relation to the exterior. Here was what looked like a fashionable hotel, complete with marble floors and tropical hardwoods. Traces of lilac wafted through the air... There were paintings on every wall, paintings in which Paola was able to recognize the work of the great Dutch and Italian masters of the sixteenth century. And none of them appeared to be reproductions...</i><br /><br />Unlike this book, which is a reproduction of several obvious bestseller approaches. The serial killing Silence-Of-The-Lambs meets the catholic-conspiratorial DaVinci-Code all wrapped up in the 'profiler' approach so well-loved by Television.<br /><br />When I was a kid I used to marvel at the million and one ways the producers of episodic tv would conspire to achieve the (apparent) Holy Grail of weekly cop shows : How To Require The Female Cop To 'Go Undercover' As A Hooker, again. This would require uncommon valor, steely resolve, and, since it was the Seventies, a halter-top with hotpants. What we have here is a little bit beyond that, but not by much.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_241152466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241152466" />
    <a title="Colleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4792989-colleen"><img alt="Colleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294785532p2/4792989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241152466?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen" href="/user/show/4792989-colleen">Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241152466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3407968718718216382">The first thing I have to say before I start my review is my immediate reaction to finishing this book: loading Wikipedia to see if it was part of a series.<br/>Sadly, I found that this wasn't part of a series - it simply left certain things hanging by a thread until 2010, three years after this book was first published, when Gomez-Jurado published The Moses Expedition, which shares two of this book's characters (at least). Perhaps in that novel we'll find out more about the characters and gain more </span>
  <span id="freeText3407968718718216382" style="display:none">The first thing I have to say before I start my review is my immediate reaction to finishing this book: loading Wikipedia to see if it was part of a series.<br />Sadly, I found that this wasn't part of a series - it simply left certain things hanging by a thread until 2010, three years after this book was first published, when Gomez-Jurado published The Moses Expedition, which shares two of this book's characters (at least). Perhaps in that novel we'll find out more about the characters and gain more answers but to be honest, for me this book is finished and I have no desire to continue reading. A prequel, perhaps, but otherwise no.<br />It's a real disappointment.<br /><br />But anyway - now for the review.<br /><br />This book started out by dropping us into the middle of all the action, but I don't think that it was handled too well. It was confusing and too open all at the same time. There is no doubt about who the killer is and not a lot of light is shed on other characters or organisations in the book.<br />Maybe I'm just stupid, but I felt that this went around in circles and strayed from the point a lot.<br />At first.<br />Later on in the book, things do begin to pick up and I found myself unwilling to put it down for any amount of time - I was staying up late to continue, being late to appointments and snatching seats on public transport so I could read in peace.<br />Then it all sort of went down hill. It was still good, but ridiculous.<br />I liked the twist at the end but it could have been handled better and I figured it out a long time before the characters did, I just assumed that if the characters weren't even considering the possibility then I must be wrong.<br />I found a lot of things I always tagged as standard police procedure being ignored - but this book is set in Italy so perhaps they do things differently.<br />I didn't feel the attraction between Fowler and Dicanti - it was sort of dropped on me every now and again like 'Oh yes, I fancy him, I remember now' but not at all consistant.<br />This book, overall, had many many bad points but I can't list them without giving away thousands of spoilers.<br />All in all though, it was interesting and gripping in a way not many books are. Despite the bad, I had to keep going to see what happened - I wanted to find out more and more about the killer because he was about the most fleshed out, believable character in it. The others were a bit flat.<br />I give this four stars for the good, which I also can't list because of the potential for spoilers.<br />I'd recommend it, definitely, but only to a certain few.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3407968718718216382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20103196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20103196" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/239204-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1186116090p2/239204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20103196?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/239204-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not even my worst enemy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/239204-linda?shelf=mystery-book-club">mystery-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/239204-linda?shelf=loathsome">loathsome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/239204-linda?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/239204-linda?shelf=couldnt-finish">couldnt-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20103196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2758343933409656098">Two cardinals are found mutilated and murdered in the days following John Paul II's death. Inspector Paola Dicanti and Father Anthony Fowler (an American priest and former army Intelligence officer) begin to suspect a conspiracy as their investigation proceeds.<br/><br/>Oh, how I hated this, and it is MY fault the book club is reading it. I know, I really do know, that I hate books with serial killers in them. Why then, did I suggest this book? I often think that the setting or characters will make up for</span>
  <span id="freeText2758343933409656098" style="display:none">Two cardinals are found mutilated and murdered in the days following John Paul II's death. Inspector Paola Dicanti and Father Anthony Fowler (an American priest and former army Intelligence officer) begin to suspect a conspiracy as their investigation proceeds.<br /><br />Oh, how I hated this, and it is MY fault the book club is reading it. I know, I really do know, that I hate books with serial killers in them. Why then, did I suggest this book? I often think that the setting or characters will make up for the utter distastefulness of the subject matter. It happens just enough to keep me hoping, but it sure didn't happen here.<br /><br />I found the main character, Paola Dicanti, to be mostly unbelievable. I had a hard time with her interactions with others and her internal dialogue. I'd say the author doesn't write women well, but the male characters are largely unbelievable, too. <br /><br />The plot turned on a few hackneyed devices: serial killer taunts the police, outwits them time after time, fixates on the female detective and sends her creepy communications, and so on. I can forgive a hackneyed plot if the characters are believable, but without that, the plot sticks out as yet another annoyance.<br /><br />Two things in this book's favor: one, the violence, though utterly disgusting, is not directed at women. There's plenty of misogyny in this book, but at least the author doesn't use the excuse of writing a book about a serial killer to glamorize violence against women. The other thing that worked, at least most of the time, was varying the plot structure. The narrative is interspersed with news reports, transcripts of therapy sessions, etc.<br /><br />The snippets from reviews on the back cover that praise this book are all from Spanish or Portuguese sources. Did something get lost in translation?<br /><br />I didn't finish it, but I read three fourths of it, then skimmed the rest. Ugh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2758343933409656098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3396544270" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3396544270" />
    <a title="KeenReader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99268936-keenreader"><img alt="KeenReader" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3396544270?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="KeenReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="KeenReader" href="/user/show/99268936-keenreader">KeenReader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780752875699" href="/book/show/1934306.God_s_Spy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/99268936-keenreader?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3396544270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6281410050549913783">First of all a warning: This book is about tracking down a serial killer who tortures and kills and it is extremely violent. In addition, a minor theme of the book concerns the sexual abuse of children. Some readers may want or need to steer well clear of it.<br/><br/>I have been thinking about how to rate this, because I really enjoyed some parts of it but was extremely irritated by others. <br/><br/>It concerns a serial killer who is preying on the priests in the roman catholic church when the successor to Pope J</span>
  <span id="freeText6281410050549913783" style="display:none">First of all a warning: This book is about tracking down a serial killer who tortures and kills and it is extremely violent. In addition, a minor theme of the book concerns the sexual abuse of children. Some readers may want or need to steer well clear of it.<br /><br />I have been thinking about how to rate this, because I really enjoyed some parts of it but was extremely irritated by others. <br /><br />It concerns a serial killer who is preying on the priests in the roman catholic church when the successor to Pope John Paul II was being chosen. It is mainly located in Vatican City and at first I suspected that the Roman Catholic/Vatican City setting was just going to be an exotic setting for a fairly standard serial killer mystery. However I was wrong, the setting was used intelligently in the book and added to the mystery (one reason for this is that it created more potential motives for the killing than would have been possible in a different setting).<br /><br />The characters were varied and well described, but one of them had a back-story that seemed very implausible to me. To make matters worse, the author referred to this background quite a lot, which irritated me, partly because I remembered the background anyway and I didn't think the frequent responses were needed. As far as I was concerned, they were definitely not wanted because every time the subject came up the background seemed less and less likely. Another problem with the characters was that at one point in the book two of them acted in ways that seemed really out of character to me. I know people can do this at times, but it was so extreme I rolled my eyes so hard I nearly injured myself. What made it worse was that the behaviour added absolutely nothing to the plot in my opinion. <br /><br />However, despite my criticisms, the mystery was interesting and unusual, thanks to the RC/Vatican City setting. It certainly kept my interest and was a pretty good page turner, even with the criticisms I have made above and I would try another book by this author. So I think 3 stars is a fair rating. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="6281410050549913783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11682110962255500858" style="display:none">This book was a bit more grisly than my usual bedtime reading, but well worth the messy bits (just read fast over them!). The Fowler character is complex and somewhat mysterious -- would have liked to know more about him. The whole Church nightmare with abusive (and abused) priests was also a "character" in the book, and all set against the backdrop of the death of John Paul II, and the conclave to decide who'd be pope next. Dicanti (female detective) was written a bit too much from a male perspective, i.e. she didn't come off as real to me.</span>

<div id="review_2171731196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2171731196" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73319768-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2171731196?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/73319768-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73319768-paul?shelf=physical">physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73319768-paul?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171731196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17973019972833563663">Although it feels initially like yet another book trying to cash in on Dan Brown's success, this novel is raised above the pack by the quality of its grounding in real history rather than surmised (it turns out that the author is a journalist so perhaps that shouldn't be so surprising) and the strong, rounded characters. It's quite grisly in places and the denouement is a little too convenient, but I found it riveting and it kept me up late on a few evenings. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2171731196">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6084788-fiona?shelf=mystery-and-spies">mystery-and-spies</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer530375415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7246253084379214570">What a suspenseful novel. After I started reading this, Pope Benedict announced that he was retiring and that the Cardinals conclave would meet to select the next pope.<br/><br/>This novel is about the killing of cardinals after the death of Pope John Paul II. Apparently, a very disturbed priest, Victor Karkosky, is doing the killing. Detective Paola Dicanti is the profiler of Rome's police and she has the help of Father Anthony Fowler who is a priest and former CIA agent. Fabio Dante is from the Corpo di</span>
  <span id="freeText7246253084379214570" style="display:none">What a suspenseful novel. After I started reading this, Pope Benedict announced that he was retiring and that the Cardinals conclave would meet to select the next pope.<br /><br />This novel is about the killing of cardinals after the death of Pope John Paul II. Apparently, a very disturbed priest, Victor Karkosky, is doing the killing. Detective Paola Dicanti is the profiler of Rome's police and she has the help of Father Anthony Fowler who is a priest and former CIA agent. Fabio Dante is from the Corpo di Vigilanza, the Vatican's high security police (not the Swiss Guards which are just "traffic cops".) Together they have to piece together where Father Victor is and stop him which is difficult because the Vigilanze, especially Dante, is often impeding the way.<br /><br />The author is a Spanish journalist. There were some bumpy English translations which did not make for smooth reading.<br /><br />Overall,good mystery.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7246253084379214570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333384523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12138031241356373261">I had been wanting to read more in Spanish, and found this as a free download. It took me a while to read, but I enjoyed it quite a bit. For those like me who are just *mostly* fluent in Spanish, it's comprehensible and fast moving. The "profiler" aspects of the story were not impressive--the killer is identified early in the story--but the emotions are real, and there are some decent plot twists. I found the end satisfying.<br/><br/>I especially liked the language, the real Spanish that you find in a bes</span>
  <span id="freeText12138031241356373261" style="display:none">I had been wanting to read more in Spanish, and found this as a free download. It took me a while to read, but I enjoyed it quite a bit. For those like me who are just *mostly* fluent in Spanish, it's comprehensible and fast moving. The "profiler" aspects of the story were not impressive--the killer is identified early in the story--but the emotions are real, and there are some decent plot twists. I found the end satisfying.<br /><br />I especially liked the language, the real Spanish that you find in a best-seller type book but not in classic literature. Makes it feel much more alive.<br /><br />It read like a movie. Probably will be one. Recommended for readers of thrillers, in the original or in translation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12138031241356373261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4629630300650820462">A friend of mine gave this to me the other day. Once I started I could not put it down. The story is set in and around the Vatican during the conclave following the death of Pope John Paul II. It was described by one reviewer as "Thomas Harris meets Dan Brown". This book is a thriller, start to finish. Very fast-paced, and very bloody. I don't normally read books that are so graphic, but I was hooked on the story from the first page. The characters were very interesting, and the author has defin</span>
  <span id="freeText4629630300650820462" style="display:none">A friend of mine gave this to me the other day. Once I started I could not put it down. The story is set in and around the Vatican during the conclave following the death of Pope John Paul II. It was described by one reviewer as "Thomas Harris meets Dan Brown". This book is a thriller, start to finish. Very fast-paced, and very bloody. I don't normally read books that are so graphic, but I was hooked on the story from the first page. The characters were very interesting, and the author has definitely left a sequel option open. (We are left with questions about Fr. Fowler's past at the end!) And who can pass up all that Catholic Church intrigue?</span>

Set in Vatican City during the conclave to elect a new pope following the death of Pope John Paul II in 2005, the action begins with the grisly deaths of two cardinals planning to participate in the conclave, their bodies tortured and mutilated almost beyond recognition by a serial killer on the loose. Gomez-Jurado is a styl</span>
  <span id="freeText4146971771914294023" style="display:none">A fast-paced thriller in which the action and blood never stop, this strong debut by Spanish author Juan Gomez-Jurado will keep many readers going until well into the night. Set in Vatican City during the conclave to elect a new pope following the death of Pope John Paul II in 2005, the action begins with the grisly deaths of two cardinals planning to participate in the conclave, their bodies tortured and mutilated almost beyond recognition by a serial killer on the loose. Gomez-Jurado is a stylish writer, well on his way to what could be a long career as a writer of thrillers. </span>

<div id="review_270357984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270357984" />
    <a title="Denise Hartman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6015701-denise-hartman"><img alt="Denise Hartman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442602614p2/6015701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270357984?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denise Hartman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denise Hartman" href="/user/show/6015701-denise-hartman">Denise Hartman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270357984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10067436326086828602">God's Spy was a good thriller and kept me interested all the way through. A few plot points I guessed wrong, so that's always fun to be surprised. I had a weird deja vu at the beginning and had to keep looking at the author to make sure I hadn't picked up a book I'd read before. Apparently I'm drawn to creepy things happening in Rome/the Vatican books, but it's been years and I enjoyed the suspense of a serial killer at work in the Holy See. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('67CuECtc/tt3tekBmBXjmOUm5QTiUP+lrAIYEXfajhTA9no3Q5P6VPvdlV23zgnoBDrzoo6n5/V7qYVY3NlWFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Guarch escoge al judío español David Meziel, nacido en 1478 y expulsado a la edad de 14 años, como protagonista de su inquisición personal. Meziel vive 80 años y su vida lo lleva desde Portugal a Túnez, y de Egipto a la corte de Suleyman el Magnífico. Muchos judíos españoles anduvieron esos caminos, otros salieron por Ámsterdam y llegaron al Báltico, o huyeron por Italia, siguiendo a las tierras del Sultán. Meziel es expulsado formalmente de España, acogido por el mundo musulmán en sus andanzas mediterráneas. Acaban de secuestrar a tu mujer. Tu día recién empieza.  Puerto Deseado, Patagonia Argentina, 1991. Raúl necesita dos trabajos para llegar a fin de mes. Cuando apaga el despertador para ir al primero de ellos, sabe que algo va mal. Su pequeño pueblo ha amanecido cubierto por la ceniza de un volcán y Graciela, su mujer, no está en casa. Todo parece indicar que Graciela se ha ido por voluntad propia... hasta que llega la llamada de los secuestradores. Las instrucciones son claras: si quiere volver a verla, tiene que devolver el millón y medio de dólares que robó. El problema es que Raúl no robó nada.  No te pierdas este thriller psicológico ambientado en una de las épocas más convulsas e inolvidables de la historia de la Patagonia: los días de la erupción del volcán Hudson.  Finalista del Premio Clarín de Novela 2018. Del autor ganador del Premio Literario Amazon 2017  SOBRE EL AUTOR: Cristian Perfumo escribe novelas de misterio y suspenso ambientadas en la Patagonia, de donde es originario. La primera, «El secreto sumergido», está inspirada en una historia real y lleva agotadas cinco ediciones, con miles de copias vendidas en todo el mundo. Además fue publicada en inglés y editada en sistema braille. En 2014 publicó «Dónde enterré a Fabiana Orquera», que agotó su primera edición en papel y en julio de 2015 se convirtió en el séptimo libro más vendido de Amazon en España y el décimo en México. En este momento, la novela está siendo traducida al francés. «Cazador de Farsantes», su tercera novela con frío y viento, también agotó su primera tirada. Su cuarto thriller ambientado en la Patagonia, «El coleccionista de flechas», ganó el Premio Literario de Amazon 2017. Su más reciente novela, titulada «Rescate gris», fue finalista del Premio Clarín de Novela 2018. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1015134661229423843">Juan Gómez-Jurado (December 1977 Madrid, Spain) is an award winning journalist and bestselling author. He is one of the three most successful contemporary Spanish authors along with New York Times bestselling authors Javier Sierra and Carlos Ruiz Zafón. In 2016, Juan celebrated the mark of 6 million readers worldwide.<br/><br/>Juan is the author of six international bestselling novels: GOD’S SPY, THE MOSES </span>
  <span id="freeText1015134661229423843" style="display:none">Juan Gómez-Jurado (December 1977 Madrid, Spain) is an award winning journalist and bestselling author. He is one of the three most successful contemporary Spanish authors along with New York Times bestselling authors Javier Sierra and Carlos Ruiz Zafón. In 2016, Juan celebrated the mark of 6 million readers worldwide.<br /><br />Juan is the author of six international bestselling novels: GOD’S SPY, THE MOSES EXPEDITION, THE TRAITOR'S EMBLEM, THE LEGEND OF THE THIEF and SCAR. They have been translated into more than 40 languages. He is also the author of the young adult science-fiction series, ALEX COLT SPACE CADET.<br /><br />Juan is an avid reader and traveller. He lives in Spain with Sam, his bad behaviored dog.</span>
